Therefore hee shortly reproueth curious heads, that search out the bottome of predestination, before they haue learned Christ, and the power of his crosse, whereas, according to the order of the Apostle to the Romanes, the knowledge of Christ must first be learned, and the mortification of the olde man, and from hence wee must proceede vnto the And then (saith he) this necessitie of predestination will waxe sweete, and we shall perceiue how full it is of consolation. the hearers must also be admonished, when any thing is spoken of it, that they abuse it not to the libertie of the flesh, or vnto desperation, hatred and blaspheming of God: but that they vse it rather to the glorie of God, and to stirre vp in them loue and care of good workes, and to vpholde their faith with all long suffering and consolation in all afflictions, by making certaine account, that there is nothing that can separate vs from the loue of God towards vs in Christ Iesu our Lord. Lastly, as touching the maner and forme of teaching it, we must take heede, that the things, which are spoken truely, be also aptly spoken, to auoide, as much as we may, the offence of the hearers. For it is greatly materiall, how, and after what maner of teaching anything is propounded. As for example, if any man speaking of predestination vnto the Church, should say, whether ye runne, or sleepe, ye shall be that, that hee, who cannot bee deceiued, hath predestinated you vnto; predestination it selfe, seemeth to bee after a sort disproued by that preaching of it among the vnskilfull; as also the foreknowledge of God (which surely no man can deny) seemeth to be blamed, if it should be saide to men, whether ye runne, or sleepe, ye shall be that, for which he, who cannot be deceiued, hath foreknowne you. More fitly to this purpose it is said: So runne ye, that ye may obtaine, and by your course know your selues to bee foreknowne, and to belong to the predestination of Gods grace. So it is too hard a saying, if a man should speake to the Christian people after this sorte: That some of you beleeue, others beleeue not, it therefore commeth to passe, because some of you haue receiued the helpe of grace, pitying your miserie, others haue not receiued it as yet. But if ye be elected, albeit not yet called, ye shall receiue the same grace. What neede is there of this speech: Some of you? For if wee speake to the Church of God, if wee speake to the beleeuers, why say wee that some of them haue receiued grace, and so are supposed to doe wrong to the rest? It may thus more fitly bee saide: thus the predestination of Gods will standeth, that ye receiuing grace, are come from vnbeliefe to faith, and that not of your selues, it is the gift of God, least any man should boast. But if any of you walke as yet in your sinnes, repent yee, awake, and rise vp from the dead. Also, if any as yet bee not called, let vs pray for them, that they may be called: for peraduenture they be so elected, that they shall be graunted to our requests, and receiue with vs the same grace. Is not thus the same thing both more truely, and more fitly spoken? Of this matter our Augustine (whom haue often cited) without controuersie a great diuine, learned, sincere, and sound, and a notable patron of the Catholike faith, (as Hilarie praiseth him) hath written more at large. To him therefore let them resorte, that desire to know these things more exactly. And these things thus farre of the eternall predestination of God, who onely is wise, mercifull, and iust. To him be honor and blessing for euer and euer: Amen. Augustine his phrase of the onely cause of all men. B. Baptisme the principall vse. Bap. of some without regeneration. by Baptisme wee are not first taken into Gods protection. Beginning of the error of the redemption of euery one. Begin in the spirit how many doe. Beleeuer knoweth himselfe to beleeue. Came for all in what sense by the old writers. Contempt of the Gospell not the onely cause of damnation. Euery one is to bee taken for a brother for his profession sake. a Fall grieuous proues not a man to be a reprobate. How he loueth and hateth vs. Hee must teach vs, els wee cannot learne. He inwardly worketh what he outwardly commaundeth, and that without sinne. They receiue the signe, but not the thing in the Sacrament. How we may resist Satan telling vs that we haue no faith. How God willeth the death of a sinner, and not. How Christs death is effectuall to vs. How mens mouthes must be stopped How Christ washeth away a mans sinnes not yet borne. the Ministerie of the Gospell hath his effect from God, not hurt by predestination. Reasons of the aduersarie, that reprobates are deliuered from the deuill. Redemption of euery one is not of the holy Ghost. Redeemed and elect some are to vs and not to God. S. Sacr. seale nothing to the vnbeleeuers Saints not to be worshipped. Satan raignes ouer the reprobates, yet they be subiect to Christ. Turkes and heathens hold many things agreeable to Christian religion. Vnbeliefe doth not condemne such as neuer heard of Christ. Vnbeliefe only damneth some that were once saued, saith Huber. Vncleane spirit cast out how he is said to returne. Weakenes of faith ought not to cast a man downe. Whether reprobates contemning the word bee in worse case then the deuils. Whether it be better neuer to heare it if it turne to their greater iudgement. Why Christ must redeeme vs with a price and not by force. Why hee came in the olde age of the world. Whole set downe for a part in these phrases, All men, All nations, &c. It cannot be taken for euery one good and bad. VVorld for the elect onely, and for the reprobates onely. World of perdition and redemption of the damned and saued. VVord of God preached alike to all, but some only profit. the Will of man is redeemed in all that be redeemed. Faults escaped in the print, are thus to be corrected. reade deluder. p. l. last saue one, for misteries reade masters. for is twise. r. are. p. l. r. please p. l.
